< Text>
The treat and great here is not a typical one. You will be asked if this is your first time or not, the staff will pleasantly walk with you throughout.

Your experience will be unique regardless. During my visit, I would hear other new commers would come, sit, eat and uncontrollably shout out "the food is great."

Very true. Mine was too. From seafood, to meat and veggi bowls. So yummy and delicious. The selections are massive. The food is so fresh and well put together.

The place is very clean and response time is within minutes and there is of course deserts a d shakes.

Mike who ownes the place managed to step away and tell me about the place that opened six years ago and become the icon of the city.

I saw a marked coin being tossed around. I found out that it is a token of thank you to the customers. Neat touch.</Text>

< text>
I love this place!
It's a great place to get a quick bite, although it's usually packed here because I'm guessing a lot of people love this place like I do.
So with their signature sandwich called the Wicked, I've mostly stopped going to Subway.
This place is great because it has more options like the olive salad, pesto dressing, crispy onions, and some other items.
In addition to having these additional toppings/dressings, they also have a lot of different sandwich options (although don't ask me about them because all I ever want from there is the Wicked).
The ingredients have always been fresh. Their toasters work. They have a loyalty program too.
Should you pick this option for your lunch some day? Yes! Of course! I'm sure that after one try you'll fall in love with this place.<//text>

< review>
I like the customizable options, and there's really something for everyone- white bread, wheat bread, lettuce wraps, and salads! They also sell individual pieces of cake, and have real ice cream shakes that look good as well. The sandwiches are toasted by default, but if you want it cold, you can ask them to just toast the bread, and not the whole sandwich. The workers are friendly and helpful. If you're a newbie to the process, that's okay, they'll explain things to you!<//review>

If you know this part of Lake is that there's TONs of parking between Lake and Mentor ave, and most stores have doors facing both Lake and the parking lots. There's seating outside, up front on Lake  blvd, for people watching, there's seating upstairs for when it's full of cal tech kids or lunch time. Lots of choices for people with all kinds of tastes. Check out their website and menu for signature sandwiches which are featured for a limited . Defiantly worth a try in this post Subway world</review>

< Text>
I absolutely love these vets. I have been to a few of the staff but my experience yesterday was unbelievable. My dog Sophie was diagnosed recently with an enlarged heart. I could see the effects it was having on her. Yesterday I rushed her over to community in temple city because she couldn't even walk and was breathing 100 miles an hour. Dr. Tsugawa immediately grabbed her and put her on oxygen and gave her a shot of Lasix. Within 30 minutes (and 15 of it giving her CPR I found out), she died. I almost didn t make it in time. I was obviously devastated but Dr. Tsugawa was amazingly compassionate and assured me they did everything they could. I knew when I put her in the car that it was extremely serious. I can't say enough good things about the Dr. Throughout the illness, with each checkup, she was amazing. Kudos to her for her bedside manner and trying her hardest to save my Sophie.< /Text>

Lori said, "Well, they typically like to have all the vaccinations current" and I replied, "but is it required." After Lori made some more sound effects, and told me that all vaccinations are required for boarding (information I did not inquire about). I clarified if this is policy or personal feeling, she said it was policy.
Lori proceeded to tell me with an attitude that they (Community Companion) told her (my mother) to come back the next day to get the cat neutered, and she (my mother) never came back, and hasn't come back since she got the cat from them. Dr Pavlik agreed that I can return the unopened medications, and we would be refunded.

Moved to Tracy California last February. Haven't been able to find a decent fully equipped good Vetrinary whatsoever. Stumbled upon Four Corners Vetrinary Hospital via internet research for an FIV friendly vet.

The minute we walked into the door we were treated with respect and given their full attention. Sweet Erica carried my cat carrier into the exam room and helped prepare Chance for his exam. She wasn't affaired or disgusted to pet and handle and FIV positive homeless pet cat we rescued from down town streets a week ago. Chance was very dirty his long hair fur coat was severely matted and knotted. He was covered with feces, urine, fox tail and dead fleas and their waste.

Regardless of how Chance looked he was treated with compassion and love. Dr, Terry lovengly and throughly examined Chance. He took his time and explained with full details everything he was doing. He even demonstrated on fake skull what was going on with Chance and gave me printed out material to take home. Chance with admitted for only day to be given IV fluids, shaved and bathed. They did a beautiful job turning Chance into a handsome Tom cat.

I highly recommend this Vetrinary hospital. Not only they are fully equipped and have a beautiful and super clean facility. But they truly go out of their way to treat the animals with compassion and respect. Dr, Terry was very experienced, informative and thorough as well. It felt like I was talking to a kind father who was teaching his child.  THANK YOU SO MUCH DR. TERRY P. KUBICKA for making my visit pleasant and for treating my homeless cat with compassion and respect. Also for the treatment and the plan, Chance is feeling much better. And I hope he will be able to fight his illnesses and live a long, healthy and happy life.

They also take care of the tiny details that does matter for my pet safety and to ease the pet fears. Most vets in Tracy don't even think about such important details to comfort the pets under their care.   You can't imagine how frustrating it was for me to beg other vets to put a towel on the ice cold and slippery stainless steel examine table. And the get the dirty look from the staff or the vet themselves.

At Four Corner Vetrinary Hospital. They cover their cold examination tables with rubber mats. Then they also put a towel that had been sprayed with relaxing pheromones to ease the pets fear and anxiety. They emphasis that one of their goals is to provide a pet hospital that is fear free for our beloved pets. They also call you the next day to check on your pet. And they have a pet portal on their website where you creat a profile for your pet and can access your pet records.
Sincerely THANK YOU SO VERY MUCH.<//Text>

,

As a hospice nurse, I find your request to have us pay for euthanizing our much- loved pug Butter rather shocking

We would like to emphasize that we witnessed our pug die a horrific, painful death at the hands of you and your technician.
In your letter you mentioned that Butter was given a standard dose of Telazol.  However, you fail to mention the exact dosage. On your letterhead you have Butter weighing in at 2 lbs more than her actual weight.
After receiving the injection of Telazol, Butter did not go into an excitement phase,  as you claimed. She did not have an unpredictable response.     Butter went into an induced agonal respiratory distressed that is common in brachycephalic breeds.  You should have been prepared for this.
Instead you left the room, had to be summoned back, observed what was taking place, took your time to have your tech check her for responsiveness. This part of the scenario especially angers me.  You should have put Butter out of her misery immediately, but at that moment, I was too emotionally devastated to say so.
We am requesting that you inform us of  the exact dosage of Telazol and any other medications given to Butter that day. We want you to provide the standard veterinary precautions that should be taken into account for flat nosed breeds when given any kind of sedation.
We stand by the fact that the euthanizing procedure you employed was improperly administered by you and your staff.

We will considering pay the $90 charge as long as you provide an invoice reflecting an accurate account of the service that was provided , not euthanizing but a careless  botched job.

Most pet owners know that putting a dog or cat under anesthesia gets riskier the older the animal is. But many people aren‚Äôt aware that genetic differences among breeds and even a dog‚Äôs anatomy can also increase the risk of anesthesia.
For example, the ‚Äúsmashed in‚Äù faces of brachycephalic breeds put those pets at higher risk for airway obstruction than breeds with longer muzzles.
Then there are breeds predisposed to increased responsiveness to anesthesia. This means it takes less of the drug to produce the desired effect, which increases the risk for overdose. There are also breeds that take much longer to recover than other animals.
Another high risk group for anesthesia is pets with heart disease. If heart problems, either acquired or congenital, are known or suspected to exist, a veterinary cardiologist should be consulted before a procedure requiring anesthesia is performed.
The purpose of the following information is to make pet owners and caretakers of these breeds aware of the potential for anesthesia-related risks. Certainly your veterinarian and his or her staff should also be aware of breed-related sensitivities and take all necessary precautions before, during and after anesthesia. But as an informed pet owner, you can provide a double layer of protection in the care of your beloved four-legged companion.
Brachycephalic Breeds
Most brachys (for example, bulldogs, pugs, boxers, Boston terriers, as well as cats with ‚Äúpushed in‚Äù faces) have some degree of brachycephalic airway syndrome. The stress placed on the airways from the use of anesthesia can result in additional airway contraction, which can cause obstruction.
Brachycephalic pets must be closely monitored from the point of premedication through the final step of extubation. Extubation (removal of the breathing tube) shouldn‚Äôt be attempted until the pet is awake, alert and swallowing. Removing the tube while the animal is still groggy from anesthesia increases the risk for upper airway obstruction.
Unfortunately, many brachys are overweight or obese and must be ventilated while anesthetized. One way to reduce your brachy‚Äôs anesthesia risk (and increase his overall quality of life) is to keep your pet at a healthy weight.<//Review>

It seems like no matter what you order, it looks and tastes great!  Today I had a skillet omelet that had sun dried tomatoes, asparagus tips and feta cheese.  I ordered the small version with 2 eggs instead of 3 and it was plenty.  I ordered the Jinky's potatoes, but my brother's tater tots looked better.

Even the decaf coffee was great!  Usually, decaf always tastes like "half" flavored coffee - like someone pours half a cup of hot water in it to reduce the caffeine, but Jinky's decaf tastes better than most places regular coffee.

Okay, it's kind of pricey, but their food is at a whole different level, so it doesn't hurt as much.

< Review>
The strangest service I have ever encountered in a restaurant.  We seated ourselves, waited some time to have someone bring us menus.  The menu is huge and food choices almost too numerous to read through.   We ordered coffees, a different person brought us coffee.  But no serving utensils on the table, we asked, and yet a different person brought us those.  Then our waitress took our order, and yet another person - completely different than the 4 previous staff - brought us our food.  Forget the idea of knowing just who is helping you - apparently this is their intended mode of serving operation, and frankly, it doesn't work.  And was slow and not attentive.   To Jinky's credit, the food was excellent.  Fix the service component please.<//Review>
